ellerbeshannon fred harris reid mcbride john k melton billy wallace jr council members ____________ mike smith town administrator preface this a complete republication of the ordinances of the town of cheraw south carolina of a general and permanent nature source materials used in the preparation of the the 1971 as supplemented no 201008 adopted on  and ordinances subsequently adopted by the commission the source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof the absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this volume the reader can locate any section of the 1971 as supplemented and any subsequent ordinance included herein the chapters of the been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage footnotes which tie related sections of the which refer to relevant state laws have been included a table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the included at the back of this volume numbering system the numbering system used in this the same system used in many state and municipal codes each section number consists of two component parts separated by a dash the figure before the dash referring to the chapter number and the figure after the dash referring to the position of the section within the chapter thus the first section of is numbered 21 and the third section of is 33 under this system each section is identified with its chapter and at the same time new sections or even whole chapters can be inserted in their proper place simply by using the decimal system for amendments by way of illustration if new material consisting of three sections that would logically come between sections 51 and 52 is desired to be added such new sections would be numbered 511 512 and 513 respectively new chapters may be included in the same manner if the new material is to be included between chapters 10 and 11 it will be designated as care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters new articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or in the case of articles may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject and in the case of divisions may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject the next successive number being assigned to the article or division the page numbering system used in this a prefix system the letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume the number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion in the case of a chapter of the the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter in the case of an appendix to the the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix the following are typical parts of codes of ordinances which may or may not appear in this this time and their corresponding prefixes charter cht1 charter comparative table chtct1 cda1 tables cct1 charter index chti1 cdi1 indices the indices of the been prepared with the greatest of care each particular item has been placed under several headings some of the headings being couched in lay phraseology others in legal terminology and still others in language generally used by municipal officials and employees there are numerous cross references within the indices which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which he is interested looseleaf supplements a special feature of this which the attention of the user is especially directed is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing for the this system the be kept uptodate periodically upon the final passage of amendatory ordinances they will be properly edited and the appropriate page or pages affected will be reprinted these new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages each such amendment when incorporated into this may be cited as a part hereof the successful keeping of this todate at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the volume as revised sheets are received it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions it is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and in addition that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference 201705 1102016 omit 4 201802 11142017 include 4 general provisions footnotes  1  editors note adopted feb 9 201 repealed the former ch 1  1118 and enacted a new ch 1 as set out herein the former ch 1 pertained to similar subject matter see also the table how cited the ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the ordinances town of cheraw south carolina and may be so cited  definitions and rules of construction in the construction of this all ordinances of the town the following definitions and rules of construction shall be observed unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council computation of time the time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last day  provided however that if the last day of the period so computed is a saturday a sunday or a legal holiday such day shall be excluded and the time period shall run until the end of the next day which is not a saturday sunday or legal holiday council town council governing body the terms the council town council and governing body shall mean the town council of the town of cheraw county the term county shall mean the county of chesterfield state of south carolina delegation of authority whenever a provision appears requiring the manager of a department or other officer of the town to do some act or perform some duty it shall be construed to authorize the manager of the department or other officer to designate delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the required act or make the required inspection unless the terms of the provision of section designate otherwise gender words importing one gender shall include the other genders unless the context indicates otherwise month the word month shall mean a calendar month name of official board commission or agency the name of any officer board commission or agency when appearing alone shall be construed as if the words of the town of cheraw were added number words used in the singular include the plural and the plural shall include the singular oath the word oath shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which by law an affirmation may be substituted for an oath and in such cases the words swear and sworn shall be equivalent to the words affirm and affirmed or and or may be read and and and may be read of if the sense requires it owner the word owner applied to a building or land shall include any part owner joint owner tenant in common tenant in partnership joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the whole or of a part of such building or land person the word person shall include a corporation firm partnership association organization and any other group acting as a unit as well as an individual personal property the term personal property includes every species of property except real property as herein defined preceding following the terms preceding and following shall mean next before and next afterward respectively property the term property shall include real and personal property public place the term public place shall mean any park cemetery school yard or open space adjacent thereto and any river or other waterway real property real estate the terms real property and real estate shall include lands tenements and hereditaments residence a persons residence is his domicile domicile means a persons fixed home where he has an intention of returning when he is absent a person has only one domicile for voting purposes a person has changed his domicile if he 1 has abandoned his prior home  and 2 has established a new home has a present intention to make that place his home and has no present intention to leave that place for voting purposes a spouse may establish a separate domicile  7125 of the sc laws 197 as amended roadway the word roadway shall mean that portion of a street improved designed or ordinarily used for vehicular travel shall may the word shall is mandatory  may is permissive sidewalk the word sidewalk shall mean any portion of a street between the curb line and the adjacent property line intended for the use of pedestrians state the terms the state or in this state shall mean the state of south carolina street the word street shall include avenues boulevards roads alleys lanes bridges and approaches thereto and all other public thoroughfares in the town and shall mean the entire width thereof between opposed abutting property lines  it shall be construed to include a sidewalk or footpath unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council tenant occupant the terms tenant and occupant applied to a building or land shall include any person holding a written or oral lease or who occupies the whole or a part of such building or land either alone or with others town municipality the terms town and municipality shall mean the town of cheraw in the county of chesterfield state of south carolina except as otherwise provided written in writing the words written and in writing shall include printing and any other mode of representing words and letters year the word year shall mean a calendar year  catchlines of sections the catchlines of the several sections of this intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections nor as any part of the section nor unless expressly so provided shall they be so deemed when any of such sections including the catchlines are amended or reenacted  effect of repeal of ordinances a the repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect b the repeal of an ordinance shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect nor any suit prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal for an offense committed or cause of action arising under the ordinance repealed  severability of parts of is hereby declared to be the intention of the town council that if any section paragraph sentence clause or phrase of this be declared unconstitutional by the valid judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction such unconstitutionality shall not affect any of the remaining phrases clauses sentences paragraphs and sections of this since the same would have been enacted by the town council without the incorporation in this any such unconstitutional phrase clause sentence paragraph or section  general penalty  continuing violations whenever in this or in any ordinance of the town or rule regulation or order promulgated by any officer or agency of the town under authority duly vested in such officer or agency any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor and no specific penalty is provided for the violation thereof the violator of any such provisions of this or any such ordinance rule regulation or order shall be punished by a fine of not more than $50000 or by imprisonment for not more than 30 days each day any violation of this or any such ordinance rule regulation or order shall constitute except where otherwise provided a separate offense  altering shall be unlawful for any person to change or amend by additions or deletions any part or portion of this or to insert or delete pages or portions thereof or to alter or tamper with such any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the town to be misrepresented thereby  certain ordinances not affected by in this affect any of the following ordinances 1 any appropriation ordinance  2 any ordinance levying or imposing taxes  3 any ordinance requiring licenses or imposing license fees or taxes not in conflict herewith  4 any ordinance providing for any public improvement  5 any ordinance making any assessment  6 any ordinance opening establishing or reestablishing the lines relocation closing or altering of any street or alley  7 any ordinance establishing or changing the name of any street or alley  8 any ordinance setting salaries compensation or bonds of town employees and officials or members of town boards or commissions not in conflict herewith  9 any zoning ordinance or ordinance making zoning map changes  10 any ordinance regulating subdivisions or approving subdivision plats not in conflict herewith  11 any ordinance establishing extending or contracting the corporate limits of the town  12 any ordinance continued in force elsewhere in this   13  adopting the mayorcouncil form of government  and all such ordinances are hereby recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out in length in this  administration footnotes  1  editors note adopted feb 9 201 repealed the former ch 2  21264 and enacted a new ch 2 as set out herein the former ch 2 pertained to similar subject matter see also the table article i  in general mayorcouncil form of government the form of government for the town of cheraw shall be the mayorcouncil form provided in sc et seq as amended  composition of council the governing body of the town of cheraw shall consist of a mayor elected at large and six councilmembers elected one from each of six separate districts  eligibility for office to be eligible for the position of mayor or councilmember a person shall be a duly qualified elector of the town and the county under the constitution and statutes of the state  elections and tenure a general elections for mayor and town council shall be held on the first tuesday following the first monday of november in oddnumbered years b the mayor and councilmembers shall hold office for the period of four years and until their successors shall be duly elected and qualified c terms shall be staggered so that not more than onehalf of the council and mayor shall be elected in the same general election  oath of office before entering upon the duties of their respective offices the mayor and councilmembers shall take the following oath i do solemnly swear or affirm that i am duly qualified according to the constitution of this state to exercise the duties of the office to which i have been elected and that i will to the best of my ability discharge the duties thereof and preserve protect and defend the constitution of this state and of the united states as mayor or councilmember of the town of cheraw i will equally fairly and impartially to the best of my ability and skill exercise the trust reposed in me and will use my best endeavor to preserve the peace and carry into effect according to law the purposes for which i have been elected so help me god  inauguration of members  mayor pro tempore a the newly elected mayor andor council members shall take office on the first regularly scheduled council meeting in january following the certification of the results of any general election for special elections any newly elected mayor andor council members shall take office on the first regularly scheduled council meeting immediately following the certification of the results b the council shall at the first meeting of the newly constituted council after any general election for municipal council elect one of its members as mayor pro tempore for a term of two years it shall be the duty of the mayor pro tempore to act as mayor during the absence or disability of the mayor or in the case of a vacancy of mayor    duties of the mayor a the mayor or in his absence the mayor pro tempore shall preside at all meetings of the council in the absence of both the mayor and the mayor pro tempore the council can elect by majority vote a council member to preside at the meeting b in addition the mayor shall have the following duties and powers 1 to appoint and when he deems necessary for the good of the municipality suspend or remove all municipal employees and appointive officers provided for by or under chapters 1 of the title 5 of the sc laws except as otherwise provided by law or personnel rules adopted pursuant to chapters 1 he may authorize any administrative officer who is subject to his direction and supervision to exercise these powers with respect to subordinates in that officers department office or agency 2 to direct and supervise the administration of all departments offices or agencies of the municipality except as otherwise provided by chapters 1 3 to preside at meetings of the council and vote as other councilmen 4 to act to insure that all laws provisions of chapters 1 ordinances of the council subject to enforcement by him or by officers subject to this direction and supervision are faithfully executed 5 to prepare and submit the annual budget and capital program to the council 6 to submit to the council and make available to the public a complete report on the finances and administrative activities of the municipality as of the end of each fiscal year 7 to make such other reports as the council may require concerning the operations of municipal departments offices and agencies subject to his direction and supervision  5930 of the sc laws 1976 as amended 8 all departments offices and agencies under the direction and supervision of the mayor shall be administered by an officer appointed by and subject to the direction and supervision of the mayor  5940 of the sc laws 1976 as amended  duties of the council a the council may establish municipal departments offices and agencies in addition to those created by chapters 1 of title 5 of the sc laws 197 as amended and may prescribe the functions of all departments offices and agencies except that no function assigned by law to a particular department office or agency may be discontinued or assigned to any other agency b the council shall have the right at all times to develop the duties of all officers and employees of the town and from time to time impose such additional duties as it may deem proper c the mayor and council may employ an administrator to assist the mayor in his office d the council shall adopt an annual budget for the operation of the municipality and capital improvements  compensation a the annual salary of the mayor shall be $540000 and each council members annual salary shall be $480000 b no ordinance changing such salary shall become effective until the date of commencement of the terms of councilmembers elected at the next general election following such change c the mayor and councilmembers may also received payments for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their official duties  meetings of council a regular meetings of the town council shall be held on the second tuesday in each month unless rescheduled by the mayor or changed by a majority vote of members present at any regular or special meeting each regular meeting of the council shall be called to order at  pm b special meetings of council may be held on the call of the mayor or of a majority vote of the members notice of a special meeting shall be given immediately to all available members and the media by the town clerk c all regular and special meetings of council shall be opened to the public  conference or executive sessions a town council may have conference or executive sessions as permitted by the south carolina freedom of information act at such times and in such places as may be deemed necessary and in the public interest b the reasons for the executive session must be clearly stated for the record and no public vote shall be taken upon any matter under discussion at any such session c a vote of council in a public meeting shall be necessary to call a conference meeting  quorum and rules of order a a majority of the council members serving constitutes a quorum for the conduct of business at any meeting b the mayor or mayor pro tempore shall preside except that in the absence of both the members shall elect a presiding member c except as otherwise required by state law or ordinance all proceedings of council shall be governed by roberts rules of order  voting requirements a all actions of council must be made by majority vote of the members present at a public meeting b every member of council present shall vote on every question except where required to refrain from voting by state law c the vote on every question shall be by voice vote and recorded in the council minutes by the town clerk d no member of council may leave the council chamber while in public session without permission of the presiding officer e should the vote of all present result in a tie the question shall be decided in the negative  minutes of meetings the town clerk shall keep the minutes of all meetings of council except executive sessions which shall be a matter of permanent public record it shall be the responsibility of the town clerk or his or her designee to maintain records on all town committees boards and commissions  agenda matters to be considered by council at a regular meeting must be placed on a written agenda by the chief administrative officer and publicly posted by the town clerk by noon of the day preceding the meeting  appearance of citizens any person is entitled to an appearance before council at any regular meeting concerning a municipal matter with the exception of personnel matters to be placed on the council agenda a person will be required to adhere to the following 1 persons desiring to speak must notify the town clerk or town administrator by noon of the friday before the regularly scheduled council meeting 2 persons must specify what topic they intend to speak about 3 persons will be limited to five minutes to address council the mayor or presiding officer may grant the speaker additional time if circumstances warrant it 4 persons that speak on other matters not specified will be deemed out of order and will not be allowed to continue speaking 5 mayor and council members have the right to answer questions that may be posed persons not placed on the agenda will also have the right to speak at the end of the town council meetings during a citizen comment period the citizen comment period is designed and intended to allow members of the public to provide information directly to the town council other than asking a question to clarify a statement council members will refrain from entering into a dialogue with the speaker this time on the agenda is not intended to be a discussion between town council and the speaker and should not be intended for that purpose persons wishing to make comments during this time will need to observe the following 1 person should approach the podium and state their full name and address before addressing the town council 2 all speakers must conduct themselves in a professional manner 3 all speakers will be limited to three minutes to speak this time allotment may not be transferred to anyone else the towns clerktreasurer will notify the speaker if they exceed their three minutes to talk 4 speakers will refrain from using profanity  language likely to incite violence or outbursts from the audience  language that is disruptive to the orderly process of the meeting  engaging in conversations with individual council members  making comments of a personal nature regarding others  shouting yelling or screaming 5 speakers should understand that the town council cannot deliberate on any questions presented by the speaker if the question or topic is not posted on the agenda    order of business the order of proceedings of the council shall be as follows 1 prayer 2 pledge to the flag 3 approval of minutes of the preceding meeting 4 approval of financial reports 5 special presentations 6 ordinances already in possession of the council shall be taken for a final reading 7 introduction of ordinances or resolutions 8 reports from special council committees 9 department reports 10 miscellaneous business not included in any of the preceding categories 11 citizen comments 12 executive session when applicable 13 adjournment  personal interest of members no member of council shall vote on any question of a private nature in the event of which such member is personally or pecuniary interested  special committees council may appoint a special committee to assist in or hold a public hearing for council at any time upon any matter pending before it minutes or reports of hearings by special committees shall be filed with the town clerk as public records  ordinances and resolutions a the town council shall act by ordinance in all matters required by law to be done by ordinance including 1 the adoption or amending of an administrative code or the establishment alteration or abolition of a municipal department office or agency  2 the establishment of a fine or other penalty or the establishment of any rule or regulation in which a fine or other penalty is imposed for violations  3 the adoption of budgets or the levy of taxes  4 the granting renewal or extension of franchises  5 the authorization to borrow money or issue bonds  6 the selling leasing or contracting to sell or lease any lands of the municipality  7 the annexation of property into the town limits  and 8 the amending or repealing of any ordinances listed above b in all other matters council may act either by ordinance or resolution oral or written recorded in the minutes  form of ordinances and resolutions a every proposed ordinance shall be introduced in writing and in the form required for final adoption which shall include 1 a title briefly describing the content  2 findings reasons or basis for the ordinance if desired and appropriate  3 an enacting clause  4 citation of any ordinance repealed  5 the provisions of the ordinance including section numbers if the ordinance is to be codified or amends and existing codified ordinance  6 the effective date of the ordinance  7 the approval of the town attorney as to form and the assignment of an ordinance number  and 8 space for the signatures of the mayor members of council and the town clerk b written resolutions shall be in such similar form as deemed appropriate by the town attorney  introduction and enactment of ordinances and resolutions a introduction 1 an ordinance or resolution may be proposed by any member of council 2 every proposed ordinance must be introduced in writing and in the form required for final adoption 3 a voice motion of a member of council shall be considered to be the introduction of an oral resolution which shall require no written record other than a notation of the town clerk in the council minutes a resolution proposed in writing shall be introduced in the same manner as an ordinance b enactment 1 no ordinance shall be adopted until it shall have been read two times on two separate days with at least six days between each reading 2 emergency ordinances may be adopted on one reading without notice or hearing by affirmative vote of onethird of the members present an emergency ordinance may not levy taxes relate to a franchise or a service rate and shall expire on the 61st day following enactment 3 the introduction and reading of any ordinance shall be by the reading of the title only unless full reading is requested by a member of council 4 the second reading of an ordinance shall be by title only and shall be for the purpose of passing the same to have the full force of law amendments and privileged motions are appropriate at this time and shall be made prior to the second reading 5 upon final adoption by vote of council an ordinance shall be signed by the mayor or presiding member members of council and the town clerk who shall file the original as a matter of public record 6 after the introduction of an ordinance any member of council or any citizen of the town interested therein may request a public hearing which may be held at any time designated by council prior to final adoption  article ii  clerktreasurer appointment  term  salary the town clerktreasurer shall be appointed by the town council and shall serve said office indefinitely or until a successor is appointed and qualified the clerk shall receive a salary and expenses at a sum to be fixed by council for any service performed as clerk  bond the town clerk prior to entering into the performance of the duties of the office shall enter into a bond with good and sufficient surety conditioned for the faithful and honest performance of the duties of such office the cost of such bond shall be paid by the town  general duties the town clerktreasurer shall 1 be the general accountant for the town  2 attend all meetings of the town council  3 take and maintain all official minutes of council meetings and record in a suitable manner  4 provide council all communications addressed to it town clerk  5 have charge of and be responsible for the preservation of all papers records and documents of every description pertaining to the town  6 shall be the custodian of the official town seal  7 issue all notices personal and general which the interest convenience laws and orders of the town require in the administration of its government  8 communicate to the council all information such officer may acquire which may contribute to the efficiency of the government and the welfare of the people  9 shall collect all taxes fines fees and licenses and shall pay all legal checks drawn upon the town  10 shall receive and receipt for all revenues of the town from all sources  11 shall provide a monthly financial statement to the council and any such other information as may be requested by the council  and 12 shall perform all duties that are now or may hereafter be required by law  signing and attesting ordinance and other documents the town clerk shall sign and attest all ordinances deeds contracts and other documents  removal of documents from clerks custody no original paper or document of the town shall be taken from the custody of the town clerk except upon order of the mayor or town administrator  article iii  town attorney appointment or election of town attorney there shall be elected annually by the town council at the time of the regular election of town offices a lawyer to serve as town attorney  qualifications the town attorney shall be an attorney at law and shall be licensed to practice before the highest court in the state and shall have met the provisions for and been issued a license to practice law by the authorized authority the town attorney shall have his place of business located within the corporate town limits of cheraw    term the town attorney shall serve at the pleasure of the town council and be appointed for a twoyear term    general duties it shall be the duty of the town attorney whenever called upon by the town council or when the necessity arises to give his advice and direction to the town council or any member thereof or to the town clerk and treasurer and chief of police on any and all legal questions which may arise in the course of the administration of the town government or in the discharge of the duties of their respective offices  and whenever required to do so by council he shall give his legal opinion in writing he shall draw or supervise the drawing or drafting of all ordinances and other instruments of writing relating to the business of the town when required to do so by the town councilor any member thereof shall whenever notified so to do attend the municipal court of the town and meetings of the town council shall take charge of all prosecutions of offenders and conduct the correspondence on all legal subjects which it may become necessary to investigate and generally shall be careful that the town council and officers fall into no error of law in the administration and management of the business and affairs of the town  duty to advise and assist mayor council and town officers when requested the town attorney shall give advice direction and assistance to the mayor town council standing committees and special committees and other officers duly charged with the administration of the town government the town attorney shall likewise advise and assist the police officers in the performance of their duties  prosecution and defense of actions  appearance in legal proceedings the town attorney shall prosecute and defend all civil actions in which the town may be a party and shall prosecute on behalf of the town all criminal cases in the municipal court whenever requested to do so by the mayor or council the town attorney shall appear on behalf of the town and its officers in all legal proceedings to which any have an interest as an official of the town  drafting ordinances and instruments  legal correspondence the town attorney when directed by the council or town administrator shall prepare the draft of any ordinance or instrument in writing which the mayor and council may desire and shall conduct the correspondence of the town on all legal subjects  compensation the salary of the town attorney shall be provided by the town council in the annual appropriation ordinance  article iv  town administrator appointment the mayor and town council shall appoint a town administrator and fix his or her compensation he or she shall be appointed solely on the basis of his or her executive and administrative qualifications  term the town administrator shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor and town council for an indefinite term  bond the town administrator shall enter into an approved bond in such sum as prescribed by the mayor and town council conditioned for the faithful and honest performance of such office the cost of such bond shall be paid by the town  general duties the town administrator shall be responsible to the mayor for the proper administration of the policies and affairs of the town and to that end shall have the power and authority and be required to 1 direct supervise and coordinate administrative activities and operations  2 appoint department heads with approval of the mayor and council  3 appoint other town employees with approval of the mayor  4 suspend or dismiss department heads with approval of the mayor and council  5 suspend or dismiss other employees with approval of the mayor  6 prepare and submit an annual operating budget and capital program to the mayor and council for their consideration and approval  7 have responsibility for administration of annual operating budget after adoption  8 prepare and annually update a fiveyear capital improvement program and budget  9 recommend and administer personnel policies classification compensation and evaluations for all employees  10 monitor the financial condition of the town and estimate present and future financial needs  11 prepare a quarterly analysis on personnel and administrative activities  12 prepare a quarterly analysis on the financial position of the town  13 combine or consolidate job positions within departments as necessary or prudent to maximize manpower utilization and efficiency  14 recommend and administer policies governing purchasing procedures and inventory control  15 authorize the purchase of services materials supplies and equipment which do not require the taking of bids provided such items are appropriated in the towns various fund accounts  16 authorize shifts in departmental budget line items provided overall departmental budget appropriations do not change with approval of the mayor and council  17 investigate complaints concerning administrative matters and personnel performance with the heads of departments  18 prepare and submit to the mayor and town council at the end of each fiscal year a complete annual report of the finances and administrative activities of the town  19 may with the approval of the mayor delegate to other administrative officers subject to his or her direction and supervision the authority to exercise specified duties and responsibilities as may be considered appropriate  20 provide the mayor and town council with information guidance and leadership in matters of policy determination  21 actively investigate the opportunities and position of the town in relation to grants state and countyshared services and resources and prepare the necessary documents upon approval of the mayor and council  removal from office the town administrator may be removed from office by a majority vote of the mayor and council those members voting for removal shall state their reasons for such vote the action of the mayor and council in removing the town administrator shall be final in all cases except for misconduct in office the town administrator shall receive 90 days notice of his removal or severance pay for 90 days where such removal is made effective immediately by a majority vote of the mayor and council  communication between administrator and council the town administrator shall relate to and communicate with the mayor and council on any and all problems situations and conditions which arise concerning any department or activity of the town which in the opinion of the administrator is of significance except for the purpose of inquiry the mayor and town council shall communicate directly with the town administrator in any and all matters concerning any department or activity of the town no member of town council shall give orders to any subordinate of the town administrator except in case of an emergency  article v  arts commission creation  powers a there is created in the town the cheraw arts commission b the commission shall develop promote and coordinate arts activities in the community more specifically the commission shall have the authority to sponsor cooperative planning research fund raising and public education programs to administer property and undertake other services and programs deemed necessary to encourage participation and appreciation of the arts by all citizens of the area the powers granted in this section shall be exercised only by recommendation to and with approval of the director of the department of parks recreation and cultural arts  artsdefinition the term arts is understood to include but not be limited to the performing visual and literary arts as well as the allied arts of architecture and historic preservation landscape architecture industrial design and production crafts  responsibilities it shall be the responsibility of the commission to 1 act as sponsor for programs and services made available south carolina arts commission and arts resources 2 survey artists and cultural resources in the area 3 encourage cooperation with and community support for existing organizations involved in arts activities 4 act as a clearinghouse for the collection and dissemination of information among existing arts groups by developing a mailing list and establishing a close working relationship with local new media 5 encourage the expansion of arts activities in the school curriculum 6 identify available space in the community for arts functions 7 work to secure government support for the arts at all levels 8 seek out and encourage contributions and grants to the arts from private and public sources and to receive and allocate such funds 9 maintain liaison with neighboring arts councils as well as state and federal arts commissions  membership a the commission shall be composed of 12 members to be appointed by the mayor initially by recommendation of the steering committee and subsequently by recommendation of the current commissioners commission members shall serve without compensation b the 12 members of the commission shall be residents of cheraw and the total membership shall be divided as follows 1 one representative of the cheraw parks recreation and tourism commission recommended by its chairperson 2 one representative of the chesterfield county school district administrative offices recommended by the county school superintendent 3 one representative of northeastern technical college recommended by its president 4 nine members appointed atlarge  terms the term of office shall be three years terms shall be staggered to provide for the appointment of three new members whose terms shall be effective on the fourth monday of may in each year any commissioner may succeed himself  officers immediately upon appointment of the commission it shall organize by electing an executive committee to be composed of a chairman vicechairman secretary and a treasurer the term of each office shall be one year and no officer shall serve in the same capacity for more than three consecutive terms  committees the commission shall create and the chairman shall appoint those committees deemed necessary to further its purpose and execute its authority these committee members need not be members of the cheraw arts commission  fiscal policy a the commission shall propose and adopt its budget under the direction of the director of the department of parks recreation and cultural arts the commission shall seek funds for its operation and programs from any and all legitimate sources including town county state and federal government  local regional and national business establishments  foundations  and the citizens of the community the commission shall not enter into any contracts involving financial liability or incur any indebtedness on the part of the town except upon written authority from the mayor and council but the commission shall have the power to enter into agreements with any government agency or with any private individuals or corporations for the purpose of effectuating its objectives where no liability of the town is involved b although the commission may solicit and receive donations operate concessions and accept and receive funds from government and private sources it shall not disburse any funds such funds are to be disbursed by and town  cooperation with existing commissions the arts commission shall cooperate and coordinate its activities with the parks recreation and tourism commission and other existing town and county commissions  meeting procedures meetings of the commission shall be conducted according to roberts rules of order a quorum shall consist of a majority of the members of the commission and a quorum must be present to officially conduct business minutes of the commission meetings shall be kept in written form and passed from chairman to chairman the chairman shall report at least quarterly to the mayor as to the activities programs and needs of the cheraw arts commission and further shall make such other reports as requested by the mayor town administrator or the director of the department of parks recreation and cultural arts  article vi  redevelopment commission creation  duties there is established pursuant to act 451 of 1985 of the sc general assembly a redevelopment commission with all of the powers and duties of said act  membership the redevelopment commission shall consist of seven members to be appointed by the mayor and town council members shall be appointed for twoyear staggered terms the town administrator and community development director shall serve as exofficio members  responsibility for operating commission the town council may at any time abolish the office of commissioners and assume the responsibility for operating the commission  powers a the redevelopment commission will have all powers necessary or appropriate to prevent or eliminate slums and urban blight it will prepare redevelopment plans and carry out such redevelopment projects b the commission may temporarily lease rent operate and maintain real property in a redevelopment area c with the approval of the town council the commission may also sell exchange transfer assign subdivide retain for its own use pledge or encumber or dispose of any real or personal property and enter into contracts regarding the real property d the redevelopment commission is empowered to borrow money to issue bonds and to provide security for such bonds the commission is further authorized to apply for an and accept forms of financial assistance for any source public or private  financing incentives a bonds may be issued where the principal and interest are payable exclusively from the income proceeds and revenues that accrue from the redevelopment project the bonds may be additionally secured by a pledge of any loan grant or contribution from the federal or state government a redevelopment project may also be mortgaged to secure the bonds the redevelopment commission may also do any other acts necessary convenient or desirable to secure its bonds or take any action that will tend to make the bonds more marketable b bonds of a commission are declared to be issued for an essential public and governmental purpose and together with interest thereon and income wherefrom shall be exempt from all taxes except inheritance estate or transfer taxes  issuance of bonds a prior to issuing any bonds the redevelopment commission shall publish a notice in a newspaper of general circulation any interested person may within 20 days after such publication but not thereafter challenge the issuance of such bonds by action initiated in the circuit court in the area in which the redevelopment commission is located if so such action is initiated provided the bonds are issued not later than six months after the publication the bond issue shall be conclusively presumed to be valid and binding b neither the commissioners nor any person executing the bond shall be liable personally on the bonds by reason of the issuance the bonds and other obligations shall not be a debt of the town or the state and neither the town nor the state is liable on them in no event will such bonds or obligations be payable out of any funds or properties other than those of the redevelopment commission acquired for the purposes of the community development law  redevelopment plan a the redevelopment plan by the commission should provide for land uses and building requirements that are designed with the general purpose of accomplishing a coordinated and harmonious development the development should promote health safety and general welfare of the community b the commission must submit the redevelopment plan to the mayor and town council for approval the commission shall also conduct a public hearing prior to adopting the plan c the redevelopment plan shall include the following 1 the boundaries of the redevelopment area  2 land use plan of the area  3 standards of population densities  4 land coverage  5 building intensities in the redevelopment area  6 a preliminary site plan  7 a statement of any proposed changes in zoning ordinances maps street layouts or street levels  8 a statement of the estimated cost and method of financing the redevelopment  9 a statement of necessary controls  and 10 a statement of the proposed method of relocating families displaced by the redevelopment plan  designated areas the redevelopment commission established by this article shall exercise its power within the corporate limits of the town of cheraw  article vii  municipal airport commission function and authority a budgeted revenue sources shall include revenues from the towns general fund from donations and from any state and federal government grant programs the commission shall be furnished a monthly report of the revenue and disbursements of the cheraw municipal airport by the town treasurer c the commission may solicit and receive donations andor services operate concessions and may accept and receive funds andor services from any governmental or other source but they cannot disburse any funds all funds and payment of bills for goods or services concerning the airport shall be disbursed in except upon written authority from the mayor and council but the commission shall have the authority to enter into agreements with any government agency or with any private individuals or corporation for the purpose of effectuating its objectives where no liability of the town is involved  membership  terms of office a the commission shall consist of seven regular members one of whom shall be commission be composed at any time of less than three members  animals footnotes  1  editors note adopted feb 9 201 repealed the former ch 3  30327 and enacted a new ch 3 as set out herein the former ch 3 pertained to similar subject matter see also the table purpose the purpose of this chapter is to promote harmonious relationships in the interaction between man and animal by 1 protecting animals from improper use abuse neglect exploitation and inhumane treatment and health hazards  2 delineating the animal owners responsibility for the acts and behavior of his animal at all times  3 providing security to residents from annoyance intimidation injury and health hazards by animals  and 4 encouraging pet ownership  definitions for the purpose of this chapter the following words and phrases are hereby defined animal any living creature which is commonly or actually domesticated animal control officer any person or employee of the town designated by the town administrator to administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter animal nuisance any nuisance arising out of the keeping maintaining or owning of or failure to exercise sufficient control of an animal animal shelter an establishment operated by the town for the temporary care confinement and detention of animals that come into the custody of the animal control officer at large an animal is off the premises of the owner and not on a leash or otherwise under the immediate control of a person physically capable of restraining the animal cruelty any act or omission whereby unjustifiable physical pain suffering or death of an animal is caused or permitted including failure to provide drink air shelter or protection form the elements a sanitary and safe living environment veterinary care or nutritious food in proper quantity domesticated any animal kept cared for sheltered fed or harbored or used as a pet work or as a source of food raw materials or inkind exotic animal any live monkey alligator crocodile cayman raccoon skunk fox bear sea mammal poisonous snake member of the feline species other than domestic cat member of the canine species other than domestic dog and any other animal that would require a standard of care and control greater than that required for customary household pets guard or attack dog any dog trained to attack on command or to protect persons or property and who will cease to attack upon command impoundment the taking into custody of any animal by the animal control officer or any other duly authorized representative of the town kennel the premises of any person or partnership or corporation engaged in the business of breeding buying selling or boarding dogs and cats or other fourlegged animals any person keeping more than eight such animals on his premises shall be conclusively presumed to be operating a kennel owner any person groups of persons or entity possessing keeping having charge of sheltering feeding harboring or taking care of any animal covered by this chapter private property property owned rented or leased by a resident or business public nuisance any animal found atlarge or making loud or objectionable sounds chasing vehicles or pedestrians or behaving in any manner which is deemed to be doing damage to property or to public health and wellbeing or which is known to have bitten one or more persons or which has been determined by the animal control officer to be a detriment to public health welfare or safety or that constitutes a physical threat to human beings or to other animals by virtue of its specific training or demonstrated behavior restraint when an animal is on the premises of its owner or keeper or when an animal is controlled by a leash or is under the control of an owner or a responsible person and obedient to that persons commands or when an animal is in a vehicle being driven strict voice command demonstrable control or governance of the behavior or of any animal as if said animal were controlled by a leash vicious animal an animal that has bitten any person or which displays or shows a propensity to attack bite or harm human beings or other animals without provocation any dog or cat which has bitten any person at any time shall be deemed prima facie vicious upon proof thereof  general powers and duties of animal control officer the animal control officer shall be charged with the following responsibilities 1 seeing that all dogs and cats in town are adequately inoculated against rabies and have proof thereof 2 will cooperate with the health officers of the various state governmental units and assist in the enforcement with regard to the control or of animals and especially with regard to the vaccination of animals against rabies 3 investigates all complaints with regard to animals covered by this chapter 4 enforces all local and state laws governing the care control and custody of animals covered by this chapter 5 supervises and maintains the operation of the townowned animal shelter  inspection and right of entry whenever it is necessary to make an inspection to enforce any of the provisions of or perform any duty imposed by this chapter or other applicable law or whenever the animal control officer has probable cause to believe that there exists in any building or upon any premises any violation of the provisions of this chapter or other applicable law the animal control officer is hereby empowered to enter such property at any reasonable time and to inspect the same and to perform any duty imposed by this chapter or other applicable law but only if the consent of the occupant or owner of the property is freely given or a search or inspection warrant is obtained as hereinafter provided 1 if such property is occupied he shall first present proper credentials to the occupant and request entry explaining his reasons therefore  2 if such property is unoccupied he shall first make a reasonable effort to locate the owner or other such persons having control or charge of the property present proper credentials and request entry explaining his reasons therefore  and 3 if such entry is refused or cannot be obtained because the owner or other person having charge or control of the property cannot be found after due diligence the animal control officer shall obtain a warrant to conduct a search for inspection of the property  animal control officerinterference by others no person shall interfere with hinder or molest the animal control officer in the performance of his duty to enforce this chapter  nor shall any person seek to release any animal in the custody of the animal control officer except as provide in this chapter  restraint and confinement a it shall be unlawful for the owner of any animal to fail to keep such animal under restraint or to permit such animal to run atlarge within the town limits b any animal while on a street sidewalk public rightofway or in any park public square or other public space and upon any private property without the consent of the owner shall be secured by a leash or chain no longer than eight feet in length of sufficient tensile strength to restrain the particular animal or shall be at heel and securely muzzled pet owners may walk their animals without leashes only when such animal responds to strict voice control commands of the owner and only when accompanied by the owner c no owner or custodian of any animal shall fail to exercise proper care and control of such animal to prevent the same from becoming a public nuisance d every female dog or cat in heat shall be confined in a building or other enclosure in such a manner that such dog or cat cannot come into contact with another animal except for planned breeding  concealment of pets no one shall hide conceal or aid or assist in hiding or concealing any pet owned or harbored when the pet is in violation of this chapter  keeping and displaying of animals a it shall be unlawful for any person in the town to exhibit keep or display pets animals birds of or fowl of any kind in show windows for a period longer than six hours per day b it shall be unlawful for any person in the town to exhibit keep or display pets animals birds or fowl of any kind in a manner without shading to keep such animals from the sun and providing adequate food water and ventilation for their use  limitation on the number of animals no person shall keep lodge or maintain in the same household in excess of four fourlegged animals more than one year of age in the town any animals in excess of this number may be impounded by the animal control officer this section shall not apply to premises operated by a licensed veterinarian in the conduct of his profession or to licensed kennels or pet shops  animal care a no owner shall fail to provide such persons animals with sufficient good and wholesome food and water proper shelter and protection from the weather veterinary care when needed to prevent suffering and with humane care and treatment b no person shall beat cruelly ill treat tease molest bait torment bother overload overwork or otherwise abuse an animal or cause instigate or permit any dogfight or other combat between animals or between animals and humans c no owner of an animal shall abandon such animal d no person shall give away any live animal reptile or bird as a prize for or as an inducement to enter any contest game or other competition or as an inducement to enter a place of amusement e any person operating a motor vehicle who strikes a domestic animal shall stop at once and render such assistance as may be possible and shall immediately report such injury or death to the animals owner in the event the owner cannot be ascertained and located such operator shall at once report the incident to the animal control officer or a police officer f no person shall expose any known poisonous substance whether mixed with food or not so that the same shall be liable to be eaten by any animal provided that it shall not be unlawful for a person to expose on such persons own property common poisons against household rodents and vermin g it shall be unlawful to raise or keep chickens within the town limits unless the chickens are maintained as follows 1 an annual permit fee of $2000 will be charged 2 no more than six chickens can be maintained 3 no roosters can be kept within the town limits 4 all chickens must be contained in a pen or coop constructed in a manner satisfactory to the codes enforcement officer 5 the pen or coop must be located in a backyard no closer than 25 feet of any property line 6 persons wishing to maintain chickens must have written permission from their neighbors whose property lines are within 100 feet of the chicken coop 7 any person receiving two complaints regarding the care of chickens shall forfeit the right to raise chickens and the town will take legal steps to remove the chickens from the premises 8 all of the requirements mentioned in items subsections 16 must be met in order to receive approval to maintain chickens h it shall be unlawful to raise or keep horses cattle sheep goats swine or any other farm animal or any kind of fowl other than parrots parakeets mynah birds and canaries within the town limits i it shall be unlawful to leave an animal in a closed vehicle or other enclosure for such duration or at such temperature that is potentially harmful to the animal    voluntary registration of animals a pet owners are encouraged to register their pets with the town by providing a copy of the current rabies vaccination tag for each pet b this information will assist the animal control officer in the prompt identification of the owner of any pet that might be lost impounded or injured c there will be no fee charged for this registration  keeping of reptiles or dangerous wild animals no person shall keep or maintain within the town limits any poisonous reptiles or dangerous carnivorous wild animals without first having registered such animals or reptiles with the animal control officer  squirrels and songbirds protected it shall be unlawful for any person to willfully kill or maim any squirrel or songbird or rob the nest of either provided however with the approval of the animal control officer and the police chief any person shall be allowed to kill any squirrel that has become a nuisance upon the persons premises  dead animals no person shall place or leave the carcass of any dead animal or fowl in any street alley or lot or allow the same to remain on his lot any person whose animal dies may contact the animal control officer to arrange pickup of the carcass  transporting of animals it shall be unlawful for any person or persons to transport any animal in or upon the back of an open vehicle without proper restraints so as to keep the animal within the sides of such vehicle  vicious or dangerous animal a it shall be unlawful for any person to own keep have charge of shelter feed and harbor or take care of any vicious or dangerous animal within the town limits except under the conditions set forth in this section b the police chief animal control officer or their designee shall have the authority to determine if there is probable cause to establish whether or not a dog is vicious or dangerous animal and then must notify the owner of the dog in writing that the dog has been found to be vicious or dangerous c the owners of all dogs deemed vicious or dangerous shall register their vicious or dangerous dog with the town hall of cheraw for a fee of $500 per dog which will enable them to receive a tag which must be fasten to the collar of said vicious or dangerous dog and this registration will expire on june 30 of each year d it shall be prohibited and unlawful for any person within the town to have in hisher possession any vicious or dangerous dog on the streets public rightofway public places of the town or on the premises of another at any time whether wearing collar and registration tag or not unless the vicious or dangerous dog is on an approved leash and is under complete and immediate control of a competent person and is obedient to that persons commands e all vicious or dangerous dogs will be confined within a fence with a minimum height of six feet which cannot be moved or buckled by the dog such fence should be of any material sufficient to keep the vicious or dangerous dog contained and any other dog or human out it must have a minimum square footage of 100 square feet have a life expectancy of not less than ten years and constructed in a manner that assures the dog cannot escape from the kennel under any circumstance any vicious or dangerous dog found outside the of the owners confinement fence will be seized by animal control and the court will be petitioned to find that the owner has violated this section and the court will be asked to allow animal control to take permanent possession of the vicious or dangerous dog and have it euthanized f the owner of any vicious or dangerous dog shall maintain a general liability insurance policy against liability resulting from acts of the said vicious or dangerous dog in the amount not less than $30000000 aggregate combined single limit for bodily injury and property damage this policy must be presented when registering the vicious or dangerous dog with town hall g owners of vicious or dangerous dogs may not restrain the animal whether on their property or elsewhere with a tether the vicious or dangerous animal must be housed in a secure kennel h any vicious or dangerous animal that has injured by attack a human or severely hurt or killed another animal will be impounded and the court of jurisdiction will be petitioned to order the vicious or dangerous animal be destroyed      editors note adopted nov 13 201 changed the title of  316 from vicious animals to vicious or dangerous animal restraint of guard dogs a every owner of a guard or attack dog shall keep such dog confined in a building compartment or other enclosure any such enclosure shall be completely surrounded by a fence at least six feet in height and shall be topped with an anticlimbing device constructed on angled metal braces with at least three strands of equally separated barbed wire stretched between them b in addition signs with blocked printed letters at least three inches high stating bewarethis property is guarded by a dog must be displayed on all sides of the property in easy visual access c the areas of confinement shall have all gates and entrances thereto securely closed and locked and all fences property properly maintained and escapeproof  animal wastes prohibited in certain areas a it shall be unlawful for any person to allow any animal owned by or under the supervision of said person to excrete fecal matter upon or in any privatelyowned property of others within any part of the town limits  and upon or in any publiclyowned street alley rightofway park or any other public place within the town b should such excretion take place said person shall be required to immediately remove fecal matter and dispose of in a lawful manner any person who fails to immediately remove fecal matter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and subject to the penalties outlined in section 327 of this c this section shall not apply to blind persons working with a guide dog or to those individuals with mobility diseases  noisy pets prohibited no person shall own keep and harbor any animal which by loud and frequent barking whining howling annoys or disturbs the peace and quiet of any neighborhood  condition of animal pens a all pet owners within the town limits shall maintain clean and sanitary animal pens or living quarters if an owner is warned by the animal control officer as to the unsanitary condition of his animal pen and does not comply within 24 hours by having the pen properly cleaned then such owner shall be in violation of the provisions of this chapter b if the owner fails to provide adequate and sanitary conditions for his pets then such animals shall be removed and taken into custody by the animal control officer  impounding  nuisance animals a in addition to other remedies provided in this chapter the animal control officer may seize impound and humanely confine to a local animal shelter any of the following animals 1 any animal atlarge  2 any animal not displaying a current rabies inoculation tag  3 any animal constituting a public nuisance or considered a danger to the public  4 any animal that is reasonably believed to have been abused andor neglected  5 any animal that is ill injured or otherwise in need or care  6 any animal that is reasonably suspected of having rabies  7 any animal that is charged with being potentially dangerous or dangerous where the animal control officer determines that there is a threat to public health and safety  8 any animal that a court of competent jurisdiction has ordered impounded or destroyed  or 9 any animal that is considered unattended or abandoned as in situations where the owner is deceased has been arrested evicted or evacuated from his regular place of residence b upon impoundment of an animal the animal control officer shall immediately attempt to notify the owner if the owner is unknown the animal control officer shall post a notice at the town hall the notices shall contain a description of the animal and shall state that unless reclaimed within seven days the animal will be disposed of or sold by the animal control officer at a cost covering all impoundment fees and penalty charges  redemption of impounded animals a an owner reclaiming an impounded animal shall pay a fee of $800 for each day or fraction thereof the animal has been impounded b in addition the following fees shall be charged for the impoundment of any animals for the provision of this chapter 1 first redemption of animal within calendar year$2500 2 second and subsequent redemptions of animal within calendar year$5000 c an additional fee of $2000 shall be assessed any owner whose dog is taken into custody without a current rabies tag d impoundment and boarding fees shall be considered service fees and not fines and do not relieve the owner from the penalties provided in this chapter such fees shall be utilized for animal control activities and supplies e any individual may acquire an animal from the animal control officer after all attempts have been made to contact the owner and after the animal has remained at the animal shelter for a period of seven days the individual will be responsible for paying impoundment and boarding fees for the animal f no fees shall be charged or collected for any animal that has been mistakenly taken up or impounded and any such animal shall be immediately delivered upon demand therefore to the owner or person entitled to the custody thereof  disposition of unredeemed animals all animals impounded under this chapter and which have not been redeemed or purchased as authorized within seven days of such impoundment may be disposed of in a humane manner by the county health department  rabies control a any animal which shows symptoms of rabies or which has bitten anyone shall be confined or isolated immediately by its owners or by the person having charge of the animal or by the person sheltering feeding harboring or taking care of said animal and the animal control officer shall be notified immediately the animal shall be confined in a place approved by the animal control officer and under conditions approved by him for not less than ten days the animal shall be subject to observation by the animal control officer under the auspices of a veterinarian at all times during said period b if rabies does not develop during said period then the animal shall be released to his owner if rabies does in fact develop the animal shall be destroyed by the animal control officer or the county health department in a humane manner  animal cruelty no person shall leave an animal in a closed vehicle or other enclosure for such duration or at such temperature as the animal control officer deems is harmful or potentially harmful to the animal  animal nuisance a it shall be unlawful for any animal to engage in any of the acts listed below which annoys or disturbs the rights and privileges common to the general public or enjoyment of private property on more than one occasion 1 enters or turns over garbage containers 2 walks andor sleeps on vehicles 3 habitually or continuously roams or is found on the property of another 4 creates unsanitary conditions that are offensive to sight andor smell 5 habitually or continuously barks howls or whines in an excessive manner one or more times per minute each minute during a tenminute period 6 is a dangerous animal as determined by the animal control officer 7 is diseased or dangerous to the health of the general public 8 is housed or restrained less than 15 feet from a public street road or sidewalk and poses a threat to the general safety health or welfare of the general public b animal nuisance complaints shall not be anonymous the complainant must be identified and must provide a signed written statement of complaint that identifies the offending animal and its owner if known including dates and times of offenses against the complainant upon receipt of such the animal control officer will investigate to determine that a violation of the nuisance ordinance has occurred upon determination of such the owner of the animal shall be issued a written warning to abate the nuisance if the owner fails to do such heshe may be fined as per the animal control ordinance  severability the provisions of this chapter are declared to be severable if any section sentence clause or phrase of this chapter shall for any reason be held to be invalid or unconstitutional by a court of competent jurisdiction such decision shall not affect the validity of the remaining section sentences clauses and phrases or this chapter but they shall remain in effect  it being the legislative intent that this chapter shall remain in effect notwithstanding the validity of any part  penalties any person violating provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor under the laws of the state and upon conviction thereof an offender shall be liable to a fine of not more than $50000 or imprisonment not exceeding 30 days or both each days violation of any provisions of this chapter shall constitute a separate offense  building regulations footnotes  1  editors note adopted feb 9 201 repealed the former ch 4  4143 4549 412 414 416421 and enacted a new ch 4 as set out herein the which no inspection is required pursuant to the codes adopted  inspections a all structural building electrical plumbing gas and mechanical work requires inspections b inspections are not required for required plan reviews shall be 50 percent of the total permit fee outlined in section 45  upholstered furniture restriction a no person shall place use keep store or maintain any upholstered furniture not manufactured for outdoor use including without limitation upholstered chairs upholstered couches and mattresses in any outside areas located in the following places 1 in any front yard  2 in any side yard  3 in any rear yard or other yard that is adjacent to a public street however an alley shall not be considered a public street for the purpose of this subsection  or 4 on any covered or uncovered porch located in or adjacent to any of the yards described in subsections a1 3 of this section b the interior of any fully enclosed porch including without limitation a porch enclosed by screening material that cannot be accessed from outside except door that can be locked shall not be considered an outside area for the purpose of this section c placement of upholstered furniture on balconies or porches located on the second floor or any floor above the second floor of a building is not precluded by the provisions of this section d the following shall be allowed concerning upholstered furniture 1 that such furniture was placed in an outside location in order to allow it to be moved during a move of a resident or residents or removed as part of a trash or recycling program on a day scheduled for such moving or removal 2 that such furniture was located in a yard other than a front yard and was placed in such a manner that it could not be seen from ground level by a person located on a public right of way excluding public alleys and that it was not visible by such a person unless that person took extraordinary steps such as climbing a ladder or peering over a screening fence in order to achieve a point of vantage 3 that such furniture was temporarily placed in an outside location in order that it be offered for sale at a yard or garage sale  fire department article i  fire department fire chief the town administrator with approval of the mayor and town council shall appoint a chief of the fire department who shall have full direction control and supervision of the fire department responsibility and duties a the fire chief shall be responsible for the execution of the fire safety mission of the town  shall promptly execute all orders and observe all regulations prescribed by the town and shall be responsible for ensuring that all such orders and regulations are carried out b the fire chief shall be directly responsible and accountable to the town administrator for the organization direction efficiency training discipline and morale of the fire department c the chief shall have complete control of operations and activities at the scene of a fire and control of the investigation of the cause origin and circumstances of fires d the chief shall ensure that all books records and reports are maintained according to current applicable federal state and municipal laws e the chief shall report annually to the town administrator setting forth the conditions and activities of the department and shall periodically report on other such matters as the town administrator may deem necessary f the chief shall submit to the town council an annual estimate of budgetary and other fiscal requirements of the fire department rightofway  right of entry while in the discharge of their duties the members of the fire department including the apparatus thereof shall have the rightofway in and upon the streets or public ways of the town when necessary for the performance of their duty for the suppression of fires and they shall also have the right of entry upon any private property and grounds fire services outside town limits the town shall provide fire protection services to individuals and businesses located outside the corporate limits of the town and within the cheraw rural fire protection service area as defined in a contract between the town of cheraw and the county of chesterfield and upon the terms and conditions thereof which are fully incorporated herein by reference thereto interference with fire department personnel no person or persons shall interfere or otherwise deter fire department personnel in the performance of their assigned duties and responsibilities article ii  fire service cheraw rural fire protection area and to make recommendations concerning the same b the commission shall review issues within the fire service area that will impact the level of fire service available to the area residents c the commission shall service in an advisory capacity only reporting any findings and recommendations to the mayor and town council  membership  terms of office a the commission shall consist of five regular members one of whom shall be elected chairman by the full membership b the fire chief of the cheraw fire department shall serve as one member of the commission with two other representatives appointed by the mayor and town council c two other members of the commission shall be appointed by the chesterfield county council d members shall be appointed for threeyear terms e members shall serve without compensation  meetings  rules  reports a the commission shall meet on a regular basis as decided upon by the membership b the commission shall meet on call by the chairman at a time and place so designated by the chairman c roberts rules of order shall be followed as a procedural guide for all meetings a quorum shall consist of the majority of the members of the commission and a quorum must be present to officially conduct business d the chairman may appoint such temporary committees from within or outside the membership as he may deem necessary to affect the function of the commission e reports on the level of fire service activities within the fire district should be reported by the commission to the mayor and town council at least quarterly
