certain dwellings which are unfit for human habitation due to 1 dilapidation  2 defects increasing the hazards of fire accident or other calamities  3 lack of ventilation light or sanitary facilities  or 4 other conditions rendering the dwellings unsafe or unsanitary dangerous or detrimental to the health safety or morals or otherwise adverse to the welfare of the residents of the town b the town deems it necessary to exercise its police powers to repair close or demolish any dwelling in the manner herein provided pursuant to the provisions of sc et seq as the same may be from time to time amended reserved adoption of international building section 41 definitions for the purpose of this chapter the following definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning board of adjustments and appeals a board appointed by the mayor with the approval of a majority of the council which shall have the powers described in this chapter in addition to any other powers granted to the board by this any other ordinance or act of the town dwellings any building structure or part thereof used and occupied for human habitation or intended to be so used including any outhouses and appurtenances belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith housing enforcement officer an individual appointed by the town administrator who shall have powers described in this chapter in addition to any other powers granted to the officer by this any other ordinance or act of the town owner the holder in fee simple and every mortgagee of record parties in interest all persons who have interests of record in a dwelling and any who are in possession thereof petitions complaint and hearing a whenever a petition is filed with the housing enforcement officer by any official of the town or any department head having duties relating to health fire or building regulations or to any other activities concerning dwellings in the town or by at least five residents of the town charging that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation or whenever it appears to the enforcement officer or on his motion that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation he shall if his preliminary investigation discloses a basis for the charges issue and cause to be served a complaint upon the owner of and all parties of interest in the dwelling b the complaint shall state the charges in that respect and contain a notice that a hearing will be held before the enforcement officer or his designated agent at a place therein fixed as soon as practical following the serving of the complaint the owner and parties of interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person or to otherwise give testimony at the place and time fixed in the complaint c the rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in hearings before the enforcement officer  orders determining fitness a if after notice and hearing as provided above the housing enforcement officer determines that the dwelling under consideration is unfit for human habitation he shall state in writing his findings of fact in support of the determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner thereof an order providing as follows 1 if the repair alteration or improvement of the dwelling can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling which reasonable cost is hereby determined as 50 percent or less of the value of the dwelling requiring the owner within the time specified in the order to repair alter or improve the dwelling to render it fit for human habitation or to vacate and close the dwelling as a human habitation  or 2 if the repair alteration or improvement of the dwelling cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling requiring the owner within the time specified in the order to remove or demolish the dwelling b 1 if the owner fails to comply with an order to repair alter or improve or to vacate and close a dwelling the housing enforcement officer may cause the dwelling to be repaired altered or improved or to be vacated or closed the enforcement officer may cause to be posted on the main entrance of any dwelling so closed a placard with the following words this building is unfit for human habitation the usage or occupation of this building for human habitation is prohibited and unlawful 2 if the owner fails to comply with an order to remove or demolish the dwelling the enforcement officer may cause the dwelling to be removed or demolished 3 the amount of the cost of the repairs alterations or improvements vacating and closing or removal or demolition by the housing enforcement officer together with an administrative assessment of $15000 shall be a lien against the real property upon which such cost was incurred and shall be collectable in the same manner as are municipal taxes provided however that nothing herein shall be construed as limiting any other right or remedy the town may have to collect such costs standards  conditions a the housing enforcement officer may determine that a dwelling is unfit for human habitation if he finds that conditions exist in the dwelling which are dangerous or injurious to the health safety or morals of the occupants of the dwelling the occupants of neighboring dwellings or other residents of the town b conditions may include but shall not be limited to the following 1 defects therein increasing the hazards of fire accident or other calamities  2 lack of adequate ventilation light or sanitary facilities  3 dilapidation disrepair structural defects or uncleanliness  or 4 other conditions rendering such dwellings unsafe or unsanitary dangerous or detrimental to the health safety or morals or otherwise adverse to the residents of the town service of complaints and orders complaints or orders issued by the housing enforcement officer pursuant to this chapter shall be served upon persons either personally or by certified mail returnreceipt requested if the whereabouts of the persons are unknown and cannot be ascertained by the enforcement officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence then he shall make an affidavit to that effect the serving of the complaint or order upon the persons may be made by publishing it once a week for two consecutive weeks in a newspaper printed and published in the town a copy of the complaint or order also shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint or order a copy of the complaint or order also shall be filed with the county clerk of court as a lis pendens sale of materials  proceeds if a dwelling is removed or demolished by the housing enforcement officer he shall sell the materials of the dwelling and shall credit the proceeds of the sale against the cost of the removal and demolition any balance remaining shall be deposited in the circuit court by the enforcement officer secured in the manner as may be directed by the court and shall be disbursed by the court to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of the court housing enforcement officer the housing enforcement officer is hereby authorized to exercise the powers as may be necessary or convenient to carry out and affect the purposes and provisions of this chapter including the following powers in addition to others herein granted 1 to investigate the dwelling conditions in the town in order to determine which dwellings therein are unfit for human habitation  2 to administer oaths and affirmations examine witnesses and receive evidence  3 to enter upon premises for the purpose of making examinations provided that the entries are made in a manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession  4 to appoint and fix the duties of the officers agents and employees with the approval of the town administrator as he deems necessary to carry out the purposes of this chapter  and 5 to delegate any of his functions and powers under this chapter to the officers and agents as he may designate board of adjustments and appeals the board of adjustments and appeals shall have all of the powers granted to the housing enforcement officer herein and may carry out its orders own actions or those of the enforcement officer or other officers and agents as it may designate appeals a any person receiving an order from the housing enforcement officer may within 15 days following the date of posting and service of the order enter an appeal in writing to the board of adjustments and appeals the appeal shall state the location of the property and the appellant shall state the variance or modification requested the reasons therefore the date of the notice of violations and the number of the notice the appellant shall further state the reasons hardship or conditions upon which the appeal is made b the board of adjustments and appeals shall notify the appellant at least seven days in advance of the date of the hearing set on his appeal stating the time and place of the hearing the board may consider any matter contained in the record of the housing enforcement officer and may take any additional testimony that may be offered by the appellant or the enforcement officer after the hearing on appeal the board shall report its findings of fact in support of its determination on the issues which may affirm modify or reject the finding of fact determinations and orders of the enforcement officer and shall cause such to be served upon the appellant owner c the board may establish its own rules of procedure provided the rules are not in conflict with this chapter of or the laws of the state the rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in appeals or hearings before the board d the housing enforcement officer shall not take any action on an order issued by him until after the 15day period for the owner to appeal to the board of adjustments and appeals an appeal to the board shall operate a stay of the order of the enforcement officer until the appeal is heard and the board has issued its order e any person affected by an order issued under this chapter shall have the right to appeal to the circuit court within 60 days after the posting and service of such order issued by the housing enforcement officer or within 60 days of posting and service of any order of the board of adjustments and appeals as provided in sc laws 197  311570 as amended the remedies herein provide shall be exclusive remedies and no person affected by an order of the housing enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals shall be entitled to recover any damages for action taken pursuant to any order of the enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals or because of compliance by such person with any order of the enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals supplemental provisions a the provisions of this chapter shall not abrogate the powers of any other department of the town or repeal any criminal ordinance but shall be in addition to and is supplemental to any other provision of this any other ordinance of the town the procedures enumerated in this chapter shall be the procedures followed in dealing with dwellings unfit for human habitation the provisions of any previously adopted standard housing code notwithstanding b nothing in this chapter shall be construed to impair or limit the power of the town to established by as contained in a separate business license pamphlet are adopted by reference and made a part hereof as fully as if set out at length herein special event permits purpose the town recognizes the importance and necessity of regulating special events for various reasons traffic control avoiding a nuisance to others controlling the effect on the surrounding area and the like application a this chapter shall apply to all special events in the town involving an outdoor activity on public or private property 1 all such activities must be of a temporary nature and cannot become permanent 2 all such events and activities shall be allowed only upon approval as required and the issuance of a special event permit b a special event likely to have a minor impact upon the town and its environs shall be allowed following approval by the town administrator or his or her designee examples of special events considered to have a minor impact are grand openings openair tent sales commercial promotional activities block parties and craft fairs c special events likely to have a major impact on the town and its environs shall be allowed following approval by the town administrator or his or her designee examples of such events are as follows circuses carnivals parades motion picture productions and activities with loudspeakers or amplified music systems 1 the following requirements shall apply to special events likely to have a major impact a schools churches and governmental entitles engaged in special events utilizing their own property are excluded from these requirements b in order to ensure the public safety and protection of the town of cheraw its businesses and citizens and to avoid conflict between events by assigning the same time and location to two or more events the town of cheraw may refuse or require alterations to a special event permit c the applicant must provide adequate security for the event as directed by the town of cheraw police department applicant may be required to hire sworn offduty law enforcement officers or hire private security personnel approved by the town of cheraw police department to ensure public safety d the applicant must provide adequate patting and must submit a plan for the events anticipated parting to include an exit plan for approval by the cheraw police department e special events must shut down operations no later than  pm sunday 00 pm friday events cannot begin before  am monday 00 pm on sunday f applicant must provide plan for cleanup and trash removal which must be approved by the towns codes officer g applicant must present certificates of liability insurance coverage with a minimum of $100000000 per occurrence h special event permit must be obtained and approved at least 15 days before event i the special event permit will be granted for the dates indicated in the application and applicant will be required to reapply for a new special event permit should they consider returning to cheraw during the year applicant will be limited to obtaining two special event permits during a calendar year j preparation and sale of food requires contacting the south carolina department of health and environmental control  regulation of garageyard sales and outdoor flea markets a purpose of section the purpose of this section is to protect the property and to preserve the peace and safety of the people of the town by regulation and control of garage andor yard sales and outdoor flea markets b definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning outdoor flea market means any person or aggregation congregation or assembly of vendors whether professional or nonprofessional that offers for sale trade or barter any goods regardless whether they are new used antique or handmade  and where offered for sale in open air areas garage andor yard sale means any sale operated out of onefamily twofamily or multifamily dwellings including but not limited to a sale on the premises thereof goods means any goods wares merchandise or any other personal property capable of being an object of sale as regulated herein itinerant or transient vendor means any person partnership firm corporation or association of individuals whether public or private charitable or noncharitable that does not occupy a permanent space within a flea market area but does exhibit goods and offers such goods for sale trade or barter on a day to day basis permanent vendor means any person partnership firm corporation or association of individuals whether public or private charitable or noncharitable that occupies a permanent space within a flea market area and that exhibits goods and offers such goods for sale trade or barter promoter means any person associations firm or corporation that promotes or sponsors flea market type activities by offering a space booth or area for use by vendors to display and offer for sale goods wares or merchandise for a fee or commission c general regulations pertaining to garage andor yard sales 1 prior to holding or conducting a garageyard sale a garageyard sale permit must be obtained in person at the town hall there is no charge for a permit 2 it shall be unlawful for any person family or vendor to hold more than four garageyard sales whether in the same or another location within the town during any calendar year charitable religious educational governmental or nonprofit organizations are exempt from this regulation 3 garageyard sales are allowed between the hours of  am and  pm 4 it shall be unlawful for any person to conduct such sale for a period of longer than two consecutive days 5 any goods offered for sale must be secondhand or used items owned by the persons or vendors conducting the sale and shall in no case have been purchased for the purpose of resale 6 no signs advertising such sale shall be located within a street rightofway 7 garageyard sales on commercial property are prohibited with the exception of charitable religious educational governmental or nonprofit organizations if a nonprofit organization desires to conduct a garage sale on property not its own the nonprofit organization must present to the town a letter from the property owner authorizing the nonprofit organization to conduct a sale on the property the letter must include the property address the name of the nonprofit organization sponsoring the garageyard sale and the dates the garageyard sale is to take place and must be signed by the property owner the nonprofit or charitable organization must also present to the town documentation that the organization is a certified nonprofit or charitable organization d general regulations pertaining to outdoor flea markets 1 any person or other vendor seeking to promote or operate an outdoor flea market in the town shall file with the town administrator an application requesting a permit to conduct an outdoor flea market type activity this application shall include complete information concerning the promoters or operators the proposed location of the sale the date and time when sale is to be conducted and any other information deemed necessary by the town administrator or his designated representative if in the judgment of the town administrator such an activity will not be to the detriment of the town or its citizens and not contrary to zoning or building regulations or other town ordinances he shall be authorized to issue a permit if in the opinion of the town administrator such will be to the detriment of the town or its citizens or will constitute a zoning or building code violation he shall notify the applicant stating the reasons for the denial of the permit  and the applicant shall have the right to appeal the denial to the town council 2 any applicant who shall have obtained a valid permit from the town administrator to conduct an outdoor flea market shall secure from the town a business license to conduct such activity for the purpose of procuring a business license the promoter or vendor shall be deemed to be a commissioned merchant the fee for such a business license is $50000 per year 3 location of an outdoor flea market will be limited to general commercial gc and limited industrial li zoned districts in the town 4 applicants desiring to hold an outdoor flea market must present a letter from the property owner authorizing such use of the property 5 outdoor flea markets may remain open for business between the hours of  am and  pm for a maximum of two days per week 6 when an outdoor flea market type activity is sponsored or promoted by a recognized civic nonprofit or charitable organization and where it is deemed that the overall interest of the town will be served waiver of the license then the council may in its discretion waive any requirements or fees associated with the operation of an outdoor flea market 7 the town council has the right to revoke any license or permit if the outdoor flea market becomes a public nuisance which includes but is not limited to the following accumulation of any garbage or rubbish becomes a visual blight significant deviation from the original intent becomes a public safety hazard including but not limited to fire and flood hazards or creates a situation where the use interferes with parking or traffic both vehicular and pedestrian  editors note adopted oct 13 201 set out provisions intended for use as  92 to south carolina department of transportation careless operation of a vehicle a it shall be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle without care and caution in full regard for the safety of persons and property any person failing to do so shall be guilty of careless driving or riding the operation of any vehicle when the same or any of its appliances is not in proper or safe condition shall be prima facie evidence of the careless driving or riding  careless operation is unlawful and may be a lesser included offense of reckless driving b it is a misdemeanor for any person to do any act or fail to perform any act required in this chapter parking heavy vehicles on town streets prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended on any street within the town activities closer than 500 feet or drive into or park such vehicle within a block where the emergency vehicle has stopped in response to the emergency whichever is greater parking of heavy vehicles in town a parking of commercial vehicles and buses in residential districts prohibited 1 no person shall park store or knowingly permit any person to park or store a commercial vehicle on any street road all roads within the town limits of cheraw as defined in subsection f below trucks as defined in this section are not allowed in the no truck zone unless they are delivering to or taking on freight from a business located within the no truck zone truck means a vehicle which either a has six or more tires or b that has a gross weight of 20000 pounds or more truck route means designated roads that trucks use to travel around the no truck zone b penalties a violator of any provision of this section shall upon conviction be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be subject to the following connecting highway 9 to highway 52 along the western side of cheraw and the truck route along the eastern side of cheraw connecting highway 1 and highway 52 to a point where those highways rejoin highway 1 and 52 and highway 9 exceptions to this will apply to trucks traveling cheraw area to destinations inside the town of cheraw they may enter the no truck zone to deliver or pick up freight from businesses located in the town limits using the most direct route d trucks making deliveries or pickups inside no truck zone trucks are allowed to enter the no truck zone to deliver to or pick up freight from businesses located within the zone such trucks must have a bill of lading which verifies the point of delivery or pickup e intracity conveyance every truck conducting intracity conveyance shall use the most direct route from the point of original within the town limits to the destination inside the town limits all trucks based at a town business leaving cheraw shall use the most direct route from the point of origin to sc highway 9 and us highways 1 and 52 f no truck zone trucks are prohibited from traveling the following sections in town 1 that section of west greene street s13146 included as  107 see also the table display of motorized vehicles for sale in residential areas a displaying of motorized vehicles for sale will be limited to one vehicle per lot in residential areas b motorized vehicles includes automobiles boats motor cycles rvs personal watercraft scooter noncommercial trailers pieces of motorized lawn equipment etc c maximum length of time a motorized vehicle can be displayed for sale is 30 days  engine compression brakes prohibited a definitions engine compression brakes means the use of the engine and transmission to retard the forward motion of a vehicle by compression of the engine engine compression brakes are also referred to as jake brakes b no person shall use engine compression brakes anywhere within the town of cheraw unless the brakes are muffled it shall be an affirmative defense that said unmuffled engine compression brakes were applied in an emergency to protect persons andor property c this section will not apply to fire engines ambulances aid trucks police vehicles and any other emergency vehicles  municipal court established there is hereby established a municipal court for the town of cheraw which shall be a part of the unified judicial system of the state of south carolina pursuant to act no 480 of 198 for the trial and determination of all cases within its jurisdiction municipal judge a each municipal judge shall be appointed by the council for a term set by the council of not less than two years but not more than four years and until his successor is appointed and qualified b the council shall notify the south carolina court administration of any persons appointed or reappointed as municipal judges c before entering the discharge of the duties of his office each judge shall take and subscribe the oath of office prescribed by of the south carolina constitution d the compensation of the municipal judge shall be as from time to time determined by council e vacancies shall be filled in accordance with sc  eligibility for judgeship  vacancy in office and temporary absence a a municipal judge shall not be required to be a resident of the town of cheraw the town may contract with any other municipality in the county or with the county governing body to employ the municipal judge of the other municipality or a magistrate to preside over its court b in case of a vacancy in the office of municipal judge a successor shall be appointed in the manner of original appointment for the unexpired term c in case of temporary absence sickness or disability of a municipal judge the court shall be held by a judge of another municipality or by a practicing attorney or some other person who has received training or experience in municipal court procedure who shall be designated by the mayor and take the prescribed oath of office before entering his duties clerk of court the police department shall designate a clerk of the municipal court who shall keep such records and make such reports as may be required by the municipal judge or the state court administrator powers duties and jurisdiction of municipal court the municipal court shall have jurisdiction to try all cases arising under the ordinances of the town the court shall also have all such powers duties and jurisdiction in criminal cases made under state law and conferred upon magistrates the court shall have the power to punish for contempt of court by imposition of sentences up to the limits imposed on municipal courts the courts shall have no jurisdiction in civil matters maximum penalties that court may impose  restitution  contempt a whenever the municipal judge finds a party guilty of violating a municipal ordinance or state law within the jurisdiction of the court he may impose a fine of not more than $50000 or imprisonment for 30 days or both b in addition a municipal judge may order restitution in an amount not to exceed $500000 in determining the amount of restitution the judge shall determine and itemize the actual amount of damage or loss in the order c a municipal judge may hold a party in contempt for failure to pay the restitution ordered if the judge finds the party has the ability to pay disposition of fines and penalties all fines and penalties collected by the municipal court shall be forthwith turned over to the clerk for deposit to the general fund of the town appeals procedures and time limits any party shall have the right to appeal from the sentence or judgment of the municipal court to the court of general sessions notice of intention to appeal setting forth the grounds for appeal shall be given in writing and served on the municipal judge or the clerk of the municipal court within ten days after sentence is passed or judgment rendered or the appeals shall be deemed waived the party appealing shall enter into a bond payable to the town to appear and defend such appeal at the next term of the court of general sessions or shall pay the fine assessed judge to make return in event of appeal in the event of an appeal the municipal judge shall make a return to the court of general sessions as provided by sc  right to jury trial  composition of jury  jury commissioners a any person to be tried in the municipal court may prior to trial demand a jury trial and such jury when demanded shall be composed of six persons drawn from the qualified electors of the municipality in the manner prescribed by law the right to a jury trial shall be deemed to have been waived unless demand is made prior to trial b the town council shall serve as jury commissioners for the municipal court commissioners to prepare jury box the jury commissioners shall within the first 30 days of each year prepare a box to be known as the jury box and shall be composed of all names on the official list of qualified electors of the town furnished by the state election commission each year this jury box may be drawn and summoned by computer in the manner the supreme court by order directs ministerial recorder there is hereby established the office of the ministerial recorder ministerial recorders shall be elected from time to time by council and shall serve at its pleasure ministerial recorders shall have the power to set and accept bonds and recognizances and to issue summonses subpoenas arrest warrants and search warrants in all cases arising under the ordinances of the town and in criminal cases as are now conferred by law upon magistrates ministerial recorders shall have no other judicial authority and shall not be law enforcement officers prosecution in magistrates courts the town pursuant to the authority of sc laws 197  14255 may prosecute apportion of its cases in the magistrates courts of the county town upon approval by the county town council such courts are hereby vested with the authority to try and determine all cases arising under municipal ordinances or state law within the jurisdiction of municipal or violations are of a continual reoccurring or constant nature provided however that no person shall be held liable or no structure shall be declared a nuisance in the event that person does not generate enable or contribute to the occurrence of unlawful behavior by a management policy or practice personal conduct lack of control or supervision absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors 1 any structure whether commercial or residential where gambling devices slot machines punch boards or other such contrivances of similar character involving elements of chance as a consideration or any type of gambling bookmaking wagering or betting is carried on and all gambling equipment except where such specific form of gambling is permitted by applicable law  2 any structure whether commercial or residential operated as a bawdy house house of assignment place of prostitution or used and maintained for the commercial or criminal purposes of unlawful sexual used for maintaining such a place  4 any structure whether commercial or residential where acts of sale possession or distribution of controlled substances occur in violation of federal state or local law  5 any structure whether a commercial operation or residential use where breaches of the peace disorderly conduct or offenses against the person found in title 16 of the sc laws offenses against the person as may be found in the town with such disproportionate frequency when compared to frequency of law enforcement action required at other similarly situated structures or where the intensity of law enforcement response when required is disproportionate to the intensity of response required at other similarly situated structures after notice of the continuing nature of the nuisance and specific identification of the facts and circumstances that either generate enable or contribute to the nuisance the owner lessee renter management of the person in control may be held responsible for the maintenance of a public nuisance and the structure declared a public nuisance a for purposes of subsection b5 only a commercial operation is defined as activity in which goods or services are exchanged for money or barter or the rental or lease of accommodations for any length of time less than 30 days  a residential use is defined as singlefamily residences or multifamily residences it is the intent of this chapter that commercial operations shall be held responsible which generate enable or contribute to the requirement of frequent or excessive law enforcement action due to a management policy or practice personal conduct lack of control or supervision absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors when such management policy or practice personal conduct lack of control or supervision absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors are identified by law enforcement as generating enabling or contributing to the disproportionate need for frequent or intensive law enforcement action notice shall be provided to the commercial operation  such notice shall identify with particularity the management policy or practice personal conduct lack of control or supervision absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors that contribute to the intensity of unlawful behavior and that further occurrences may result in the declaration of a public nuisance if after notice the management policy or practice personal conduct lack of control or supervision absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors that are generating enabling or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior are not changed or modified the owner lessee renter management or the person in control may be held responsible of the maintenance of a public nuisance and the structure declared a public nuisance b for the purpose of subsection b5 only a residential use is defined as any residence in which a family or individual or individuals reside for a period exceeding 30 days it is the intent of this chapter that owners lessees or renters of property shall be held responsible for the conduct of the residents invitees or guests that generate enable or contribute to the requirement of frequent or intensive law enforcement action when conduct is identified by law enforcement as generating enabling or contributing to the disproportionate need for frequent or intensive law enforcement action notice shall be provided to the owner lessee or renter  such notice shall identify with particularity the conduct that is generating enabling or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior and that further occurrences may result in the declaration of a public nuisance if after notice the conduct that is generating enabling or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior is not changed or modified the owner lessee renter management of the person in control may be held responsible and the structure declared a public nuisance c nuisances affecting public welfare and safety the following are hereby declared to be public nuisances affecting public welfare and safety 1 all trees hedges signs or other obstructions or any portion of the same so located on private property which prevent persons driving vehicles approaching an intersection of streets from having a clear safe view of traffic approaching such intersection  2 all trees hedges signs or other obstructions or any portion of the same so located on private property which prevents the clear and unobstructed view of a fire hydrant structures for a period of one month which remain unoccupied and boardedup and whose exterior finish is destroyed decayed dilapidated or deteriorated in violation of the international property of appearance and security according to the international property maintenance the material which secures the building is compatible with the exterior in appearance color texture and design and the premises are kept in compliance with all applicable building property maintenance zoning and land use laws  3 all businesses or commercial enterprises operating without a valid current and displayed business license  4 all premises continually not in compliance with applicable licensing zoning and land use laws  5 all businesses with an outstanding arrearage of applicable town liens taxes fees charges or assessments  6 all premises which originate false fire or burglar alarms as defined by applicable law e junk generally it shall be unlawful for any person or firm including an owner or occupant of any premises dwelling or structure or vacant lot to place or leave or permit to be left outside of any premises building or lot any dilapidated furniture icebox refrigerator stove or other appliance machinery equipment building material or parts thereof or other item which is wholly or partially rusted wrecked junked dismantled or inoperable f junk yards it shall be unlawful for any person or firm to do business as a junk dealer for any such junk materials including discarded vehicles machinery metal objects and other such commodities unless the same be kept and stored within or beneath a covered screened or enclosed structure or in such other manner as prevents threat or occurrence of injury or damages by way of nuisance to the health or welfare of the public it shall also be unlawful to deposit or leave such junk or permit such junk to be deposited or left on the public rightofway in conjunction with such business g noise 1 generally subject to the following provisions of this section the creation of any unreasonably loud disturbing or unnecessary noise in the town is prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person to cause make or contribute to creating any loud or disturbing noise of such character intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any individual or such noise as to disturb the quiet and peace of any citizen in the town 2 unlawful acts enumerated the following acts among others are declared to be loud disturbing or unnecessary noises and are not specifically prohibited by this section the following shall not however necessarily include all such noises as may constitute a violation of subsection 1 of this section a blowing horns the sounding of any horn whistle signal device on any motor vehicle except as a danger signal or as required by law so as to create any unreasonably loud or harsh sound or the sounding of such device for an unreasonable period of time is hereby prohibited b sirens the use of any bong bell or siren on any motor vehicle other than police fire rescue or other emergency vehicle permitted by law is hereby prohibited c sound amplifying devices the playing of any radio stereo compact disc player record player tape recorder television musical instrument or soundproducing or soundamplifying device in such manner or with such volume as to annoy or disturb the quiet repose or comfort of any person in any dwelling hotel or other residence is hereby prohibited d blowing whistles the blowing of any steam whistle attached to a boiler except as a warning of danger to give notice to start or stop work or as an indicator of time is hereby prohibited e noises to attract attention the use of any bell drum loudspeaker or other instrument for the purpose of attracting attention by the creation of noise to any performance show sale display or advertisement of merchandise is prohibited f exceptions the foregoing provisions of this section shall not apply to organized and lawfully permitted performances by bands groups etc in parades or otherwise or to the conduct of manufacturing operations as defined by the south carolina department of revenue or the conduct of lawfully permitted vehicle races g emergency situations noise caused in the performance of emergency work for the immediate safety health or welfare of the community or individuals of the community or to restore property to a safe condition following a public calamity shall not be subject to the provisions of this section other nuisances the enumeration of specific nuisances in this chapter shall not be deemed to make lawful any other act or condition declared to be a nuisance by any other town ordinance state or federal law or court decision reporting emergencies and emergency actions any person who directly observes a nuisance posing an emergency threat to the health or safety of the environment shall immediately report the incident to the cheraw police department and shall provide any information requested by the law enforcement officer needed to investigate or abate the potential emergency if any nuisance exists in such a condition so menacing to the public health peace or safety that it is necessary that it be summarily abated the town enforcement officer after consultation and concurrence with the town administrator may proceed to abate the nuisance without a hearing nuisances prohibited and unlawful no person shall create any public nuisance in the town and no person shall by inaction permit a public nuisance to occur or continue on any real property under such persons control whether by recorded or unrecorded instrument or permission nor shall any person permit a public nuisance to occur involving any personal property under such persons control institution of criminal process and penalty the public nature of a public nuisance must be made by an enforcement officer or other appropriate governmental official enforcement of this chapters provisions may be accomplished upon the institution of criminal process by way of uniform traffic ticket municipal ordinance summons or warrant made only by a law enforcement officer or appropriate government official each day of violation constitutes a separate misdemeanor offense subject to a fine not to exceed $50000 and or up to 30 days imprisonment for each offense in its discretion the town may elect to use
